### [ ] [score 5.5] Vitest coverage CI gate — add per-workspace thresholds to lock in the post-test-drive completeness
- proposed: 2026-05-19, expand pass 17
- source signals:
  - **Commit-pattern signal (G — 22+ consecutive test commits)**: The systematic test-coverage drive spans passes 14–17. 22+ paired audit+test commits addressed every previously untested foundational module across all 6 workspaces — `@thock/data`/`@thock/content` loaders and caching contracts, validation infra (`walkAll`, `validateAll`, `paths.ts`), MDX components (Callout, Caption, PullQuote, PartReference, ArticleBody, Source.tsx), quiz orchestrator, search runtime (SearchPanel), Trends Tracker helpers. This is the longest single-category iterate drain in the project history. No vitest config has a `coverage` section — new code can ship without tests and the iterate loop catches it reactively (audit notice → file row → drain = 2–3 ticks per gap).
  - **Post-drive completion signal (this pass)**: The current iterate audit found no F-category (test) findings ≥ 3.0. This is the first tick since pass 14 where coverage is genuinely current across all workspaces. The natural engineering response to "we just filled all coverage gaps" is a gate that prevents them reopening.
- rationale: Without a threshold, every new phase that ships code without unit tests goes undetected until the next iterate audit. With per-workspace thresholds, CI fails immediately when a new commit introduces uncovered code — catching it in the same tick instead of 2–3 ticks later. The 22+ drain commits demonstrate the value: proactive enforcement would have prevented most of that drain. Proposed starting thresholds (statements 60%, functions 70%, lines 65%) are conservative enough to not block any current phase's shipping pattern while still catching "zero tests for new feature" cases. Per-workspace (not global rollup) so thin packages like `tokens` aren't held to the same bar as `packages/data`.
- proposed scope (1 phase):
  1. Add `coverage: { provider: 'v8', reporter: ['text', 'html'], thresholds: { statements: 60, functions: 70, lines: 65 } }` to all 6 vitest workspace configs. Thresholds calibrated per-workspace against current coverage snapshot at implementation time — the numbers above are starting estimates; the implementer adjusts to green before committing.
  2. Add `pnpm test:coverage` script at root workspace: `vitest run --coverage` across all workspaces. Additive alongside `pnpm test:run` — verify gate retains `test:run` (faster, no v8 overhead); CI calls `:coverage` separately.
  3. Add a `coverage` step to `.github/workflows/march.yml` (or new `coverage.yml`) that runs `pnpm test:coverage` on push to `main`. Runs in parallel with deploy-check; a threshold failure surfaces as a CI annotation without blocking the deploy.
  4. `plan/bearings.md` "Verify gate" section: one-liner noting the coverage thresholds so future phases know new code needs tests.
- estimated phases: 1
- conflicts: none — additive only; verify gate (`pnpm verify`) is unchanged; no URL contract change; no schema change.

### [ ] [score 6.5] Critique gate diagnostic — `/critique` has not fired in 53 days / 1091 commits despite Step 2's dispatch condition being trivially satisfied on every cloud tick
- proposed: 2026-07-03, digest (first nightly pass)
- source signals:
  - **Pulse signal (dominant)**: `plan/CRITIQUE.md`'s header reads "Last pass: 2026-05-10T20:35:00Z at commit 931c8a7 / Pass count: 11" — unchanged as of this digest, 53 days and 1091 commits (`git rev-list --count 931c8a7..HEAD`) later. `skills/march.md` Step 2's dispatch condition is an OR of three sub-conditions ("current commit ≥12 commits after Last-pass commit, OR Last-pass >24h ago, OR Last-pass 'never' + phase 5+ shipped") — the ≥24h leg alone has been true on every cloud tick since roughly 2026-05-11T20:35, yet the header never advanced past pass 11.
  - **Ruled out (B — process of elimination against march's own logged conditions)**: (a) Step 1 triage preemption — `GH_TOKEN` is unavailable in cloud per essentially every expand-pass signal-audit note in this file ("triage unavailable (GH_TOKEN unavailable in cloud)"), so Step 1 always falls through to Step 2 on cloud ticks; (b) a blocked HIGH critique row — expand-pass signal audits have read "CRITIQUE.md 0 Pending rows" on nearly every pass across the window, so Step 2's condition 3 (don't preempt an in-flight HIGH drain) isn't the blocker; (c) a red deploy — `pnpm deploy:check` has read green at every digest/expand checkpoint spot-checked in the window.
  - **Independent of the concurrent march outage**: the 10-day march blackout (2026-06-23 → 2026-07-03, see `plan/DIGEST.md` "While you were out") only explains the most recent 10 days. The critique gate was already ~44 days / ~950 commits stale *before* march ever stopped ticking — this is a standing mistuning of the gate itself, not a symptom of the outage.
- rationale: With triage-preemption and the HIGH-row-block both ruled out and deploy green throughout, Step 2's OR-condition should have dispatched `/critique` on the very next eligible tick after 2026-05-11T20:35, and then repeatedly every ~12 commits or 24h thereafter — hundreds of eligible cloud ticks in the window. It never did. Two live hypotheses: (a) an implementation bug in how Step 2 is actually evaluated at runtime — possibly related to the same skill file describing the cadence as "≥12 commits + ≥24h spacing" (read as AND) in its own Purpose section while Step 2's body spells out an OR, an internal inconsistency that could be resolved either way depending on which was actually implemented; or (b) `/critique` is being dispatched but silently no-op'ing or erroring before it can update the `plan/CRITIQUE.md` header, with the failure swallowed non-fatally. A months-stale fresh-eyes queue is exactly the blind spot `/critique` exists to prevent — roughly 1091 commits of site surface area have shipped unreviewed by an external-observer pass.
- proposed scope: 1 phase — (1) resolve the Purpose-section-vs-Step-2-body ambiguity (AND vs. OR) to a single unambiguous condition, matching whichever cadence was actually intended; (2) add a one-line trace log inside Step 2 (e.g. an appended run-log line: "critique gate evaluated: <bool>, reason: <condition-that-fired-or-didn't>") so the next multi-week gap is diagnosable from run logs instead of inferred after the fact from a stale header; (3) manually trigger one `/critique` pass to break the freeze and re-baseline `plan/CRITIQUE.md`'s header; (4) if the freeze recurs after (1) and (2) ship, that isolates the fault to `/critique` itself rather than march's dispatch condition, and narrows the next investigation to `skills/critique.md`.
- estimated phases: 1
- conflicts: none — skill-file + logging change only; no route/schema/URL contract change.

### [ ] [score 6.0] march.yml crash-issue gate never fires when the action itself fails — implicit `success()` swallows the one case it exists for
- **update (2026-07-05, iterate cloud tick)**: wrote and verified the two-line `always()` fix, then discovered it can't be pushed from cloud at all — see the new sibling candidate below ("Cloud loop cannot push `.github/workflows/*.yml` changes"). The fix itself is unchanged and ready to apply verbatim once that's resolved; not re-diagnosing here.
- proposed: 2026-07-05, digest (this pass)
- source signals:
  - **Direct reproduction (dominant)**: run `28721452962` (2026-07-04T22:19:29Z, `conclusion: failure`) shows step 9 "Run /march (cloud mode)" failing after 2s with no transcript. Step 10 "Inspect execution for problem signals" (`if: always() && ...`) correctly ran and logged `has_issues=true` / `has_transcript=false` to `$GITHUB_OUTPUT` (confirmed via `gh run view --job ... --log`). Step 12 "Open GitHub issue for problematic execution" — whose only stated condition is `if: steps.inspect.outputs.has_issues == 'true'` (`.github/workflows/march.yml:249`) — nonetheless shows `conclusion: skipped` in the same job. No "Cloud march tick crashed" / "Cloud march execution had issues" issue exists for this run (`gh issue list --state all --search crash` returns only the unrelated `#1` from 2026-05-09, already closed).
  - **Root cause (GitHub Actions semantics)**: per Actions' own `if:` evaluation rules, a custom condition that doesn't reference `always()`/`failure()`/`cancelled()` gets an implicit `success()` prepended. Steps 11 and 12 (`.github/workflows/march.yml:239-249`) both lack it, so once step 9 fails, the job's running status is already non-`success()` and both steps skip regardless of `has_issues`. Step 10 avoids this only because it explicitly opens with `always()`. This is exactly backwards for step 12: the one execution class it exists to surface (the action crashing outright) is the one class where the job is already non-`success()`, so the gate silently no-ops precisely when it matters most. It correctly fires only for the "action exited 0 but the transcript shows denials/is_error/api_error" case — a real but narrower slice of "problematic."
  - **Blast radius confirmed narrow this window**: of the 30 most recent `march` runs, only this one failed at the action step; the rest succeeded, so the gap has cost exactly one silently-unsurfaced crash in the sampled window — but it is a deterministic, 100%-reproducible miss for that entire failure class, not a flaky one-off.
- rationale: The comment block directly above these steps (`.github/workflows/march.yml:178-184`) states the intended contract explicitly — "A problematic tick uploads the transcript and opens a single issue linking to it" — and the crash-before-transcript branch is the first case handled in the inspect step's own logic (lines 194-205), so the gate was clearly designed to cover exactly this scenario. The fix is a one-line-per-step change (`always() && steps.inspect.outputs.has_issues == 'true'` on both steps 11 and 12), not a redesign — low risk, mirrors the `always()` already present on step 10.
- proposed scope: 1 phase — (1) add `always() &&` to the `if:` conditions on `.github/workflows/march.yml` steps 11 ("Upload Claude execution transcript") and 12 ("Open GitHub issue for problematic execution"); (2) manually re-run or simulate a forced-failure tick locally (or via `act`/a scratch workflow dispatch) to confirm the issue now opens on an action-step failure; (3) no test suite covers `.github/workflows/*.yml` today — a one-line note in the workflow's own comment block documenting the `always()` requirement is the durable guard against regressing this same gap on a future edit.
- estimated phases: 1
- conflicts: none — workflow-file change only; no route/schema/URL/skill-file contract change; does not touch the verify or deploy gates.

### [ ] [score 5.5] Cloud loop cannot push `.github/workflows/*.yml` changes — no PAT/App scope currently satisfies GitHub's workflow-write restriction
- proposed: 2026-07-05, /iterate audit (cloud march tick)
- source signals:
  - **Direct reproduction (dominant)**: attempted to ship the sibling [6.0] march.yml `always()` fix this tick. Wrote the two-line diff, ran the full verify gate green (typecheck, 591 web unit tests, data:validate, build, 959/959 e2e), committed locally, then `git push origin main` failed: `refusing to allow a GitHub App to create or update workflow ".github/workflows/march.yml" without "workflows" permission`. Had to `git reset --soft` + revert the file rather than leave an unpushed commit.
  - **Credential inspection**: in this session, `GH_TOKEN` and `GITHUB_TOKEN` env vars are identical (`ghs_`-prefixed GitHub App installation tokens) and match the token embedded in `git remote -v`'s push URL. This means the push credential is the ephemeral Actions-provided App token, not the `ACTIONS_PAT` secret the workflow's own comments describe using for git identity/`gh` CLI purposes (`.github/workflows/march.yml:50-52` sets it via `actions/checkout`'s `token:` input, but evidently the App-token default is what git actually authenticates with for the push, or `ACTIONS_PAT` itself also lacks the `workflows` scope — either way, no credential available to the cloud loop can currently write `.github/workflows/*`).
  - **GitHub platform semantics**: GitHub enforces a distinct `workflows` permission (separate from `contents: write`) specifically for any push that creates or modifies a file under `.github/workflows/`. Fine-grained PATs need this explicitly granted; classic PATs need the `workflow` OAuth scope. Neither `secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN` (Actions' auto token) nor, apparently, `secrets.ACTIONS_PAT` as currently scoped satisfies it.
- rationale: This isn't specific to the march.yml crash-gate fix — it's a standing capability gap. Any future cloud-discovered improvement to a workflow file (this one, `digest.yml`, `night.yml`, etc.) will hit the identical wall. Two independent fixes exist: (a) regenerate/re-scope the PAT backing `ACTIONS_PAT` to include "Workflows: write" (fine-grained PAT permission), and confirm the `checkout` step's `token:` input is what git actually uses for push (may need an explicit `git remote set-url` or credential-helper step rather than relying on `actions/checkout`'s default behavior); or (b) accept the constraint and route all `.github/workflows/*.yml` edits through local `/oversight` only, documenting this in `agents.md`/`CLOUD_LOOP.md` the same way brand-setup taste calls are gated. Both are cheap; (a) restores full cloud autonomy, (b) is zero-effort but permanently caps what cloud ticks can fix.
- proposed scope: 1 phase (or a same-tick `/oversight` decision, not a full phase) — (1) user decides (a) vs (b) locally, since checking/regenerating a PAT's scopes and confirming the push-credential path needs a local session with token-management access the cloud loop doesn't have; (2) if (a): re-scope the PAT, verify with a scratch workflow-file edit + push from a cloud tick; (3) if (b): add a one-line note to `agents.md`/`.github/CLOUD_LOOP.md` under cloud-mode adjustments — "workflow-file edits are local/oversight-only; cloud ticks that discover a workflow bug file the fix as a blocked AUDIT.md row instead of shipping it."
- estimated phases: 1 (or zero, if resolved as a same-session `/oversight` credential fix rather than a phase)
- conflicts: none — infrastructure/permissions decision, not a product/content/schema change.

### [ ] [score 7.0] Automated content-fact-vs-catalog numeric-spec audit — cross-check article prose citations of spring weight / actuation weight / tracker scores against the data records they cite
- proposed: 2026-07-14, expand pass 192; score raised 6.5 → 7.0 + evidence extended at pass 209
- source signals:
  - **Commit-pattern signal (G — 5 near-identical fix cycles in a 15-commit window)**: since pass 191 (8614276), the loop shipped 5 separate "article cites a wrong number from the catalog/tracker" fixes, each its own content+audit commit pair: `d369778`/`8589230` (building-mode-sonnet-with-oil-kings — wrong Oil King bottom-out spring weight), `2160a6b`/`bd4db77` (drop-holy-panda-x-deep-dive — wrong Oil King spring weights), `cee903d`/`34f26bc` (computex-2026-keyboard-highlights — wrong W21 hall-effect tracker score), `0d8d9f3`/`2090366` (rapid-trigger-gaming-crossover — W21/W22 sparkline label mismatched against its own cited score), `8633c9c`/`24401d8` (spring-swaps-explained — wrong HMX Cloud actuation weight). A sixth adjacent fix in the same window, `564abb6`/`bd4db77` (durock-t1-deep-dive — "five-year-old" claim off by a year), is the same failure class one level up (a stale-relative-to-`releasedAt` claim rather than a stale-relative-to-`springGrams` claim).
  - **Pass-209 addition — the class now spans newsletters, and survived a partial fix**: open issue #566 (filed by the same-shape audit sweep, still `loop:opened`, not yet drained) reports `thock-weekly-001.mdx` and `thock-weekly-002.mdx` both citing a fabricated "eight weeks ago" Hall Effect/Rapid Trigger tracker figure — the row didn't exist 8 weeks before either snapshot week, and the real elapsed time (4–5 weeks) is quotable directly from `data/trends/2026-W21.json`'s inception score. The issue notes an *earlier* partial fix (`3fd26a8`) already corrected the same "eight weeks ago" phrasing class on issues 003/004 but missed 001/002 — evidence that this is a durable recurring shape best caught by a scheduled cross-check, not one-off manual sweeps that don't guarantee full corpus coverage.
  - **Existing-pattern gap (H — every other recurring content-accuracy class already has a survey script, this one doesn't)**: `scripts/article-language-check.mjs` catches stale present-tense phrasing; `scripts/article-parts-check.mjs` (shipped phase 38) catches missing `mentionedParts` cross-references; `scripts/group-buy-status-check.mjs` catches stale group-buy `status`/`endDate`. None of the three — nor any other survey — cross-checks a *numeric value* an article states in prose (a spring weight in grams, an actuation-force number, a tracker score) against the ground-truth field in `data/switches/*.json` (`springGrams.actuation`/`springGrams.bottomOut`) or `data/trends/<week>.json` (`rows[].score`). Every one of the 5 instances above was found by a manual Explore-agent sweep, not a scheduled check — the identical shape that motivated the already-Pending `[6.0]` external-link-rot-survey candidate (line 209 above), just for numbers instead of URLs.
  - **Same-category audit density (A)**: all 5 fixes filed under `plan/AUDIT.md` category `content`, scores 4.0–5.4, addressed across passes 191→192 in near-immediate reactive succession (a fix ships, verify goes green, the next tick's audit sweep finds the next one) — the reactive-discovery pattern itself is the signal that a proactive check would collapse into fewer ticks.
- rationale: Each instance follows the same mechanism: an article cites a switch's spring weight, actuation force, or a tracker week's score in prose, and that number silently drifts out of sync with the canonical `data/` record (either the article was wrong at write time, or the underlying data record was corrected afterward and the article's citation wasn't). This is structurally identical to the already-shipped `article-parts-check.mjs` (which cross-checks *presence* of an entity reference) and the already-Pending stale-group-buy-frontmatter candidate (which cross-checks *status* prose against a linked record) — the missing piece is cross-checking *numeric value* prose against a linked record. A script that (1) resolves each article's `mentionedParts` switches, (2) regexes the article body for gram/force values near each switch's name or alias, (3) diffs found values against that switch's `springGrams.actuation`/`springGrams.bottomOut`, and equivalently for tracker-score citations against `data/trends/<week>.json`, would catch this mechanically at ship time instead of one Explore-agent sweep at a time.
- proposed scope: 1 phase — new `scripts/content-fact-audit.mjs` (mirrors `article-parts-check.mjs`'s resolve-then-diff shape): for each article, resolve `mentionedParts` switch slugs, regex-scan the body for "<N>g" / "<N> gram" / "<N>-gram" patterns within a short token window of the switch's name/alias, compare against that switch's `springGrams` fields, flag mismatches; equivalently resolve any `W\d\d` tracker-week token near a numeric score mention and compare against `data/trends/<week>.json rows[].score`. Files `content` category AUDIT rows on mismatch (mirrors `group-buy-status-check.mjs`'s scoring: ease 8–9 once a mismatch is found since the fix is a one-line prose correction, impact 4–5 since it's a factual-accuracy concern on published content). Wire into `skills/march.md` §3b.5a's survey chain (after `og-coverage-check.mjs`) and `skills/digest.md`'s nightly breadth check, `--write`-gated and best-effort like every sibling survey. Pass-209 scope note: extend the same regex-scan-then-diff pass to `apps/web/src/content/newsletters/*.mdx` (issue #566's surface), not just `apps/web/src/content/articles/*.mdx` — the "N weeks ago" relative-time phrasing needs its own diff rule (resolve the cited entity's real first-appearance week in `data/trends/` and compare against the snapshot week's own `publishedAt`, rather than a static numeric-field compare). No schema, component, or URL contract change.
- estimated phases: 1
- conflicts: none — pure script addition following the established survey-script pattern (mirrors `article-parts-check.mjs` and `group-buy-status-check.mjs`, both already precedented); runs read-only against existing data + content, writes only to `plan/AUDIT.md`.

- estimated phases: 1
- conflicts: none — additive CSS default + new script; no URL contract change; no data schema change; existing focus-ring classes on already-fixed surfaces are superseded, not broken.

### [ ] [score 5.5] ship-data entity-arrival mentionedParts rescan — prevent N-tick lag when new catalog records land
- proposed: 2026-06-20, expand pass 131
- source signals:
  - **Commit-pattern signal (G — 14 `fix:` mentionedParts commits in 23-commit window)**: Since pass 130, 14 of 23 commits (61%) are mentionedParts `fix:` commits touching 7 articles. Root cause: when `ship-data` adds a new entity record (gmk-cyl-selene, gazzew-boba-u4t, keychron-q1-he), existing articles that already mention that entity by name are not rescanned. The iterate loop discovers the stale mentionedParts 1–3 ticks later and drains them one-by-one — 2 commits (audit + fix) per article. The 14-commit batch represents ~7 articles × 2 commits = 14 ticks of loop time.
  - **Audit queue residual (A — 2 remaining mentionedParts [3.6] rows)**: The 2 remaining AUDIT rows in this window are both mentionedParts gaps triggered by the same post-Phase-38 entity additions. They confirm the structural lag still fires on the current corpus.
- rationale: `article-parts-check.mjs` has a `--write` (full corpus scan) and gate mode (named files). It lacks an `--entity <slug>` filter that returns only articles mentioning a specific entity name. Adding this flag enables `skills/ship-data.md` Step 4 to run `article-parts-check.mjs --entity <slug> --write` immediately after adding a new switch/keycap-set/board record — filing AUDIT rows for any existing articles mentioning the new entity in the same ship-data commit. This collapses the 14-commit drain into 0 extra commits (the AUDIT rows land at add-time; iterate drains them on the next content tick alongside other work, not as a dedicated standalone batch). The 14-commit batch is the concrete signal; the fix is a one-shot script CLI extension + skill amendment.
- proposed scope: 1 phase — (1) add `--entity <name>` CLI flag to `scripts/article-parts-check.mjs` (filter catalog to the named entity; scan all articles for that entity's name in prose; file AUDIT rows for gaps); (2) one Vitest/node:test unit test (`--entity GMK CYL Selene` on a mock corpus with 1 violating + 1 clean article → files 1 row); (3) amend `skills/ship-data.md` Step 4 (after writing the entity record): run `node scripts/article-parts-check.mjs --entity "<name>" --write`, and if rows are filed, commit them as a follow-up `audit:` commit in the same tick. No URL contract change, no schema change, no component change.
- estimated phases: 1
- conflicts: none — additive CLI flag; `--write` default behavior unchanged; no route or data schema change.

- [score 3.5] Tracker link href snapshot enforcement — extend Phase 36 language gate to detect bare `/trends/tracker` hrefs in article MDX body (without a `/YYYY-WNN` week suffix). Pass 28 window drained 12+ articles where `/trends/tracker` links resolved to the live W21 tracker instead of the W19-era snapshot matching the article's cited scores. Phase 36's gate catches forbidden prose patterns but not link target staleness. Fix: add `"pattern": "\\(/trends/tracker\\)"` (matching link syntax `[text](/trends/tracker)`) to `scripts/article-language-patterns.json`. One-line addition; iterate-shaped. Corpus is now clean; prevention closes the gap for future /ship-content articles. Added pass 28. **Pass 30 signal update (2026-05-25):** `7662ecb fix(copy): zmk-mainstream-shift` surfaces a second variant — article referenced the tracker for a topic (ZMK/wireless firmware) that has never appeared in any `data/trends/*.json` snapshot; the fix removed the bare tracker href entirely (topic not tracked, reference was misleading). Two variants now: (A) bare href citing stale week-specific scores, (B) bare href for untracked topic. **Pass 31 signal update (2026-05-25):** `b9c9bfc fix(copy): alice-layout-decline` surfaces a third variant — article body said "down 18 percent on the W19 tracker" with no hyperlink at all (the citation existed as text but had no href). Three variants now: (A) wrong href (bare `/trends/tracker` for week-specific citation), (B) bare href for untracked topic (href removed entirely), (C) no href on historical citation (link needs to be added). Variants A and B are prevented by the pattern-match addition; variant C requires a different approach (detect "W19 tracker" or "tracker snapshot" prose without accompanying href) — distinct lint rule, still iterate-shaped. Score unchanged at 3.5. Note: "Follow the [trends tracker]..." closing lines in group-buy articles use bare tracker hrefs intentionally (forward-looking directives, not historical citations) — any prevention pattern must carve out this form. **Pass 33 signal update (2026-05-26):** `af530a7 fix(copy): hall-effect-mainstream` surfaces a fourth variant — article published W17 (2026-04-22) used "At publication, the [Trends Tracker] showed..." but the tracker did not exist until W19 (2026-05-06); the qualifier is anachronistic, claiming tracker data from before the tracker launched. Distinct from Variants A–C: the link anchor may be correct (W21), but the temporal qualifier itself is false. Prevention: add a pattern to `article-language-patterns.json` detecting `[Aa]t publication.*[Tt]rends [Tt]racker` combined with a publication-date pre-filter (articles published before 2026-05-06) — or simpler, just add the literal string "At publication, the [Trends Tracker]" as a forbidden pattern since this phrasing is almost never editorially accurate on static MDX. Still iterate-shaped; four variants now documented.

### [score —] "Find your switch" interactive recommender — phase 33 (user-requested fun phase)
- promoted: 2026-05-16 via `/oversight` (this commit) — direct user request: "Anything fun we can add as phase 33?"
- assigned phase: **33**
- the fun, on-brand pick: thock is an editorial site about a tactile hobby with an 8+ record switch catalog (`data/switches/`) reachable only via in-article rails. A short interactive **switch recommender** turns the existing catalog into a playful entry point without new data, new assets, or external services.
- promotion decisions (locked at /oversight time):
  - **Route**: `apps/web/src/app/quiz/switch/page.tsx` (+ `loading.tsx` wrapping skeleton in `<main id="main">` per the phase-22 landmark contract). Client component for the interactive step state; the catalog is read at build time via the existing data-runtime loader (no client data fetch).
  - **Mechanic**: 4–5 single-select questions — sound profile (thock / clack / silent), actuation feel (linear / tactile / clicky), hand fatigue tolerance (light / medium / heavy spring), primary use (typing / gaming / mixed), budget tier (optional). Each answer applies weighted filters/scores over `getAllSwitches()`; results render the top 2–3 matches as cards linking to their existing `/part/switch/[slug]` pages (reuses phase 21 surfaces — no new detail pages).
  - **Pure + testable**: the scoring is a pure helper in its own `.ts` module (`recommendSwitch(answers, catalog)`) with its own unit tests (deterministic ranking; "all-tactile + heavy spring" → expected top result; empty/contradictory answers → graceful fallback ordering). Component split into small files (QuizStep, ResultCard, the page) per the build-plan style guardrails — no jam-packed single file.
  - **Discovery + SEO**: sitemap entry for `/quiz/switch`; canonical-urls + page-reads fixtures extended so the smoke walker covers it; `WebApplication` or `Quiz`-flavored JSON-LD (implementer picks the closest schema.org type at brief time). Add a small "Not sure where to start? Find your switch →" affordance somewhere honest (e.g. the future `/parts` index when it lands, or the switches-tag page) — keep it to one entry point, no nav-bar churn.
  - **e2e**: `apps/e2e/tests/quiz.spec.ts` — walk the quiz (answer each step, assert a result card with a `/part/switch/` href appears), assert no horizontal scroll at 375px, assert JSON-LD shape.
  - **No analytics special-casing**: page-level GTM already covers it; respects the existing `DISABLE_ANALYTICS=1` e2e gate.
  - **Brief drafting**: drafted on-demand by `/ship-a-phase` (or pre-warm via `/plan-a-phase phase 33`). Ships after 31 + 32 in phase order — it's the fun dessert, not a priority jump.
- estimated phases: 1
- conflicts: none — new route only, no schema change, reuses phase-21 part pages + existing switch data.

### [score 7.0] Content-velocity queue auto-refill — make the Rule-1/2/3/4 content-gap queue self-replenishing
- promoted: 2026-05-14 via `/oversight` (this commit)
- assigned phase: **30**

  - **Rule 1 algorithm**: sliding 30d window per pillar; comfortable (≥2) → no row; hot pursuit (=1) → score 7.0; critical hot pursuit (=0) → score 9.5. Pillar selection on multi-cold: oldest most-recent publishedAt → lowest window count → prominence (Trends > News > Ideas > Deep Dives > Guides). Window cutoff, floor, and score values are bearings constants; helper reads from a single named-constants block (mirrored from bearings.md § Rule 1).

  - **Verify gate**: two unit tests — (a) "1 article in 30d, deep-dives" → rule=1 pillar='deep-dives' score=7.0; (b) "0 articles in 30d, news" → score=9.5 with critical-hot-pursuit framing.
  - **Brief drafting**: drafted on-demand by `/ship-a-phase`.
- original signals + scope: see git history of this file at `ceefc38^` (pass-7 row); current bearings reframe makes Rule 1 algorithm sliding-window, fully captured in the promotion decisions above.

### [score 7.0] Group-buy hero art — schema additive + retrofit + durable shipping rule

  - **Schema additive**: `packages/data/src/schemas/group-buy.ts` gets a `heroImage: string?` field (Zod additive, optional). The existing `imageUrl` field stays — that's vendor-supplied product imagery, not the loop-generated hero. `heroImage` is the loop's editorial illustration.
  - **Render surfaces**: `/group-buys` cards, home `<GroupBuysWidget>` rows, and any `<TrackerRow>` that tags a group buy. All three render `heroImage` if present; fall back to a coral-tinted placeholder block if absent (so a partial backfill doesn't leave broken-image holes).

This mirrors the article-hero rule from phases 5+ (content-curator + brander as one bundle). Phase 23 ships the amendment as part of the brief execution.

## Rejected

### [score 4.5] Article series navigation — optional series frontmatter + prev/next reader affordance

- reason: sat below the promotion line since pass 94 (~8 days, ~30 expand passes) without score movement. A `series` frontmatter concept can be re-proposed if a genuinely ordered multi-part series is ever commissioned editorially; the current corpus pattern is thematic clustering, not sequenced parts.
- user answer at /oversight 2026-06-11: "Reject the two 4.5s".

### [score 4.5] Orphan parts editorial baseline — targeted articles for catalog parts with zero editorial cross-links
- rejected: 2026-06-11 via `/oversight` (this commit)
- reason: sat below the promotion line since pass 112. Commissioning articles to serve catalog records inverts the editorial direction — content should drive data, not backfill it. Rule-1 content velocity (~1 article per 3–4 days) plus the phase 38 mentionedParts gate will organically absorb orphan parts as future articles naturally mention them; parts that never earn a prose mention don't warrant commissioned coverage. Detail pages for orphan parts remain reachable via `/parts`, kind indexes, search, and the quiz.
- user answer at /oversight 2026-06-11: "Reject the two 4.5s".

### [score 6.5] React #418 hydration flake — dedicated investigation phase
- rejected: 2026-05-11 via `/oversight` (this commit) — **self-resolved**
- reason: pass-6 status update (commit `ec8d4c0`) recorded the flake had not been observed in 10+ consecutive parallel verify runs. Confirmed via /oversight: phase 16's PageStub-to-real-page replacement (`f3e5bac`) is the load-bearing fix — once every dynamic-data route had a real page (not the stub with its client/server-divergent state), the second hydration source the dfa5596 TZ patch couldn't reach went away. Serial-fallback mitigation is no longer the established per-tick pattern. The AUDIT.md row tracking this is cleared in the same commit.
- promotion path no longer needed: no investigation phase required.
